## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics / constitutive modeling of thermo-mechanical behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly suggests a constitutive law for a solid where elastic modulus, yield/flow stress, and hardening/softening depend on temperature. Common relationships combine a strain-dependent stress response with temperature-dependent material parameters (e.g., thermoelasticity, thermoplasticity, thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermoelasticity, E varies with T)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * T) (accounts for thermal expansion strain via an effective strain shift)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Landau-type) with T-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (weakly nonlinear elasticity, symmetry-allowed odd terms)
- Exponential-modulus thermoelasticity: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (empirical strong temperature dependence of stiffness)
- Strain power-law with thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T)**c3 (hardening in strain with multiplicative softening vs T)
- Temperature-dependent hardening exponent: sigma = c0 * epsilon**(c1 + c2 * T) (T modifies the apparent strain-hardening exponent)
- Voce hardening with T-dependent saturation and rate: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (saturating flow stress with temperature-dependent levels)
- Rational saturation (smooth elastic-plastic transition proxy): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + c2 * epsilon**c3) (initially linear, then saturating/hardening)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4))**c5 (strain hardening with thermal softening relative to a reference temperature)
- Eyring/hyperbolic-sine flow proxy (thermally activated shape without Arrhenius-in-1/T): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (captures transition from linear to logarithmic-like growth and softening with T)
- Large-strain exponential elasticity proxy: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (exp(c2 * epsilon) - 1) (rapid stiffening with strain; parameters depend on T)
- WLF-type temperature shift factor applied to modulus/stress scale: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * (T - c2) / (T - c2 + c3)) (viscoelastic/time-temperature superposition-inspired temperature dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: if data show sigma proportional to epsilon at small epsilon, start with sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon where E(T) is linear/quadratic or exponential in T.
- Thermal expansion signature: if sigma changes sign/offset with T at fixed epsilon, use an effective strain form (epsilon - c * T) inside the stress law to represent thermal strain subtraction.
- Thermal softening near a reference/melting point: collapse of sigma with increasing T is often captured by multiplicative factors like (1 - c * (T - c0))**m that can drive sigma toward zero as T rises.
- Saturating plastic flow: if sigma increases quickly then approaches a plateau with epsilon, use Voce-like 1 - exp(-c * epsilon) or rational saturation epsilon/(1 + c * epsilon**n).
- Changing hardening with temperature: if curvature of sigma–epsilon changes across temperatures, allow T to modulate hardening rate or exponent (e.g., epsilon**(c0 + c1 * T) or exp(-c * T) multiplying the hardening term).
- Nonlinear elasticity at larger strain: if stiffening accelerates with epsilon, exponential-in-epsilon forms exp(c * epsilon) - 1 are a compact proxy for hyperelastic response.
- Yield/flow stress shifting with T: if curves are roughly parallel but vertically shifted with T, add a T-dependent offset term (c0 + c1 * T) plus a strain-dependent hardening term.
- Competing effects (stiffness vs softening): when sigma scales with E(T) at small strain but softens at larger strain, combine an E(T)*epsilon factor with a softening-in-epsilon factor like exp(-c * epsilon) or 1/(1 + c * epsilon**n).

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci0)

GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
Candidate formulas: 114

Let \(e=\epsilon\) and expand the GT into a clear basis of independent terms.

### 0) Ground Truth (fixed function)
GT:
\[
31.119982052994235\, e\left(-0.05295088673159155\,(T-316.1945018642116)+1\right)\;-\;0.22554447458683766\,(T-316.1945018642116)\;+\;3.629301836816963\, e^{0.5975773894779193}(T-316.1945018642116)
\]

Expand into monomials in \(T\) and \(e\):
- First big term:
\[
31.119982\,e\left(1-0.0529508867\,T+0.0529508867\cdot 316.1945\right)
= A_1\,e + A_2\,T e
\]
(no constant term, no pure \(T\) term)
- Second term:
\[
-0.22554447\,T + 0.22554447\cdot 316.1945
\]
(pure \(T\) and constant)
- Third term:
\[
3.62930184\,T e^{p} - 3.62930184\cdot 316.1945\, e^{p}
\]
with \(p=0.5975773894779193\) (a non-integer, non-0, non-1 exponent)

So GT is exactly of the form
\[
\underbrace{\alpha\,T e}_{Te} \;+\;\underbrace{\beta\,e}_{e}\;+\;\underbrace{\gamma\,T}_{T}\;+\;\underbrace{\delta}_{1}\;+\;\underbrace{\eta\,T e^{p}}_{T e^{p}}\;+\;\underbrace{\theta\,e^{p}}_{e^{p}}
\]
with **both** \(T e\) and \(T e^{p}\) present, and **both** \(T\) and constant present, and \(p\approx 0.5976\).

That structure is very restrictive: any matching candidate must be able to produce simultaneously:
- a \(T e\) term,
- a \(T e^{p}\) term with \(p\neq 1\),
- a pure \(T\) term,
- a constant term,
- an \(e^{p}\) term (without \(T\)),
- and an \(e\) term (without \(T\)).

Also, note the repeated shift \((T-316.1945)\) in GT forces the presence of paired \(T\)-and-constant contributions for the pure-\(T\) part and for the \(e^{p}\) part.

No trig/abs/log/exp identities are relevant because GT is purely polynomial-in-\(T\) and power-law-in-\(e\) with one fractional exponent.

---

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1. \(T c0\,e^{c1} + c2 + c3 e^{c4} + c5 e^2 + c6 e + c7 e^{c1} + c8 e\)
Has \(T e^{c1}\) and \(e^{c1}\), plus constant and \(e\).  
But GT needs **both** \(T e\) and \(T e^{p}\) with \(p\neq 1\). This candidate has only **one** \(T\cdot(\text{power of }e)\) term. You cannot get two different \(T e^{(\cdot)}\) powers simultaneously. ⇒ No.

### 2. \(T c0 e^{c1} + c2 e^{c3} + c4 e^2 + c5 e + c6 + c7 e^{c1}\)
Same issue: only one \(T\)-dependent \(e\)-power term. GT needs two (\(Te\) and \(Te^p\)). ⇒ No.

### 3. \(T^2 c0 + T c1 e^{c2} + T c3 + T c4 e + (c5+c6)e + c7 + c8 e^{c2} + c9 e\)
Contains \(T^2\) unless \(c0=0\). Then has \(T e^{c2}\), \(T e\), \(T\), constants, \(e^{c2}\), \(e\).  
This is promising structurally: can match \(Te^p\) via \(c2=p\), and match \(Te\) via \(T c4 e\). Also has pure \(T\) and constant.  
But GT also needs an \(e^p\) term with coefficient tied to the same shift \((T-316)\): i.e., the coefficient of \(T e^p\) and the coefficient of \(e^p\) must be in ratio \(-316.1945\). Candidate 3 has independent coefficients for \(T e^{c2}\) (via \(c1\)) and \(e^{c2}\) (via \(c8\)), so we *can* enforce that ratio by choosing \(c8=-316.1945\,c1\). Good.  
Similarly, for the pure \(T\) and constant part, GT has \(-0.2255(T-316)\) so constant and \(T\) coefficients must satisfy \(\delta = -316.1945\,\gamma\). Candidate has independent \(T c3\) and constant \(c7\), so set \(c7=-316.1945\,c3\). Good.  
For the \(Te\) and \(e\) terms: GT’s \(Te\) and \(e\) coefficients are linked through the first bracket \(31.119982 e(1-0.05295(T-316))\), which implies a specific relationship between the \(Te\) coefficient and the \(e\) coefficient. Candidate 3 has \(T c4 e\) and several independent \(e\) coefficients \((c5+c6+c9)\), so we can satisfy that too.  
**However:** GT’s \(e\) term is not just free; it is \(31.119982 e(1+0.05295\cdot316) - 31.119982\cdot0.05295\,T e\). That is exactly affine in \(T\) times \(e\), which candidate can represent with \(T c4 e\) plus constant\(\times e\). So still OK.  
Thus candidate 3 actually has enough degrees of freedom to match all required monomials exactly (with \(c0=0\), \(c2=p\), and appropriate choices of \(c1,c4,c3,c7,c8\) and the \(e\) linear coefficients).  
⇒ **Yes, candidate 3 can match GT.**

(Once one match is found, the final verdict is match; but I’ll still quickly classify the rest.)

### 4. Same as 3 but includes \(c5 e^2\)
Set \(c5=0\). Then identical capability as 3. ⇒ Yes.

### 5. Has \(T^2\) and a \(\sin(\cdot)\) term
GT has no sinusoid; cannot remove \(\sin\) unless amplitude \(c5=0\). Then still only two \(T\)-dependent \(e\)-terms? It has \(T c1 e\) and \(T c2 e^{c3}\) plus \(e^{c3}\). With \(c0=0\) it could also match similarly to 3 (it lacks pure constant shift coupling for \(e^{c3}\) unless \(c9\) provides it—yes \(c9 e^{c3}\) exists). Also has pure \(T\) via \(T c4\). So it can match too. ⇒ Yes.

### 6. Like 3 but no explicit constant \(c7\)? (it has \(c6\) constant)
It has constant \(c6\) and pure \(T c3\), so OK. Has \(T e^{c2}\) and \(T e\), and \(e^{c2}\) and \(e\). With \(c0=0\) can match. ⇒ Yes.

### 7. Same as 6 plus \(e^2\)
Set that \(e^2\) coefficient (it is fixed as \(+e^2\), not parameterized) — actually candidate 7 has a bare “\(+\epsilon^{2}\)” with coefficient 1, cannot be turned off. GT has no \(e^2\) term. ⇒ No.

### 8. \(T c0 e +\) only \(e\)-powers, constant
No \(T e^{p}\) term. ⇒ No.

### 9. Only one \(T e^{c1}\) term (plus another \(e^{c1}\) but not \(T e\) separately unless \(c1=1\), then you lose \(p\neq1\)). Cannot get both \(Te\) and \(Te^p\). ⇒ No.

### 10–11. Have \(T^2\) term removable by \(c0=0\); include \(T e^{c2}\), \(T e\), \(T\), constants, \(e^{c2}\), \(e\). Extra “\(+\epsilon\)” in 10 can be absorbed by adjusting \(c8\) etc because it’s just another \(e\) term (not fixed coefficient? In 10 it is a bare “+ epsilon” with coefficient 1, cannot be removed, but you can compensate by changing other \(e\) coefficients to still match GT’s \(e\) coefficient; since GT has an \(e\) term, having an extra fixed \(+1\cdot e\) is not an obstruction). So 10 and 11 can match. ⇒ Yes for both.

### 12–30. These are mostly “\(T c0 e^{c1} + T c2 e +\)” etc without a separate \(T e\) and \(T e^{p}\) pair in the right way, or they introduce logs/exp/extra powers of \(T\) that can’t be eliminated (unless their coefficients can be set to 0). Many could match if they effectively reduce to the same basis as candidate 3: need both \(T e\) and \(T e^{p}\) and also \(e^{p}\), \(e\), \(T\), constant.  
Most of 12–30 **lack** a \(T e^{p}\) term *and* a separate \(T e\) term simultaneously (they often have only \(T e^{c1}\) and \(T e\) but no \(e^{c1}\) term with independent coefficient, or vice versa). Some include extra non-removable nonlinearities (log/exp terms with nonzero coefficient parameter—those can be set to 0 if multiplied by a parameter).  
I won’t mark each as match/no-match since we already have a match, but key point: any candidate with only one \(T\cdot e^{(\cdot)}\) term cannot match.

### 31–50. Many have \(T^2\) removable, and include both \(T e\) and \(T e^{c3}\) plus \(e^{c3}\) and \(e\) and constants; those can be tuned similarly. Any with unavoidable trig/log/exp terms (not multiplied by a free coefficient) would fail; most are multiplied by coefficients so can be zeroed.

### 51–114. Similar story: candidates that can represent the six-term basis \(\{Te, e, T, 1, Te^p, e^p\}\) with \(p\approx0.5976\) can match; those that cannot (missing \(Te^p\) or missing pure \(T\) or constant, or having non-removable extra terms like a fixed \(e^2\)) cannot.

## Explicit constructive match (for Candidate 3)
Candidate 3:
\[
T^2 c0 + T c1 e^{c2} + T c3 + T c4 e + c5 e + c6 e + c7 + c8 e^{c2} + c9 e
\]
Choose:
- \(c0=0\)
- \(c2 = 0.5975773894779193\)
- \(c1 = 3.629301836816963\) (matches GT coefficient of \(T e^{p}\))
- \(c8 = -316.1945018642116 \cdot 3.629301836816963\) (matches \(-316\) shift for \(e^{p}\))
- \(c3 = -0.22554447458683766\) (matches pure \(T\))
- \(c7 = +0.22554447458683766\cdot 316.1945018642116\) (matches constant shift)
- For the \(Te\) term: set \(c4 = -31.119982052994235\cdot 0.05295088673159155\)
- For the \(e\) term: set \(c5+c6+c9 = 31.119982052994235\cdot\left(1+0.05295088673159155\cdot 316.1945018642116\right)\)

This reproduces GT exactly for all real \(T\) and (for real-valued power) \(e\ge 0\), which is a plausible physical domain.
